> a blanket theorem “finite-order isolated (T_v=0) boundaries are locally sterile” is false; the mixed case is a genuine codimension-two obstruction.

That is the kind of negative result that saves a lot of wasted time. It tells us not to keep pushing a false universal local sterility theorem on the lifted side. 

So, strategically, I would now update the hierarchy of attacks like this.

First priority: **formalize the two lifted sterility theorems** that now look real.

Those are:

1. finite-order isolated (K_v=0) implies local sterility for lifted (3)-point birth;
2. finite-order isolated (T_v=0) with (K_v\neq 0) implies local sterility for lifted (4)-point birth. 

Those should become theorem-level statements in the paper, because they are exactly parallel to the new (W=0) story on the one-pair side and they cleanly remove generic local lifted birth as the main obstruction.

Second priority: **make the mixed case explicit as the remaining local lifted obstruction**.

That tells the reader exactly where the local lifted route stops.

Third priority: **decide whether the actual zeta geometry can realize the dangerous mixed patterns** ((m,n)).

To me, this is now the cleanest next theorem target on the lifted side. The question is no longer generic local birth. It is:

> does the actual one-pair zeta geometry permit the mixed normal forms whose generalized Vandermonde admits opposite-side coplanar quadruples?

If the answer is no, the lifted route gets dramatically cleaner. If the answer is yes, then the mixed case becomes the one genuine local obstruction that the global endgame must carry.

Fourth priority: keep the **quantitative defect-thickened strengthened coincidence** route in parallel, but I would now treat it as the **global bridge**, not the immediate local attack.

That route is still valuable because it says bad two-pair cores force near-coincidence of the strengthened invariant (\widehat\Psi). But the new lifted summary tells us the local geometric side is now more sharply stratified than we previously thought. So I would use the quantitative coincidence theorem to force bad cores into the close-point regime, and then use the lifted stratification:

* generic close-point bad cores are killed by the (K_v)- and (T_v)-sterility theorems,
* only mixed (K_v=T_v=0) close-point cores remain.

That is a much cleaner endgame split than before. 

So my current ranking is:

1. write/prove the (K_v)-sterility theorem;
2. write/prove the (T_v)-sterility theorem under (K_v\neq 0);
3. isolate the mixed normal-form invariants ((m,n)) and test whether the dangerous patterns are realizable in the actual geometry;
4. in parallel, prove the quantitative defect-thickened strengthened coincidence theorem to force bad two-pair cores into this local lifted classification. 

That is now cleaner than the old one-pair (\beta)-route, because it replaces a vague global recurrence problem by a much more structured dichotomy: generic local lifted birth is gone, and the remaining local obstruction is a specific codimension-two mixed model.

So my bottom line is:

**Yes, this is a real advance, and it changes the route.**
The lifted finite-core story is no longer just “another possible approach.” It now gives the sharpest map of the remaining local obstructions, and I would lean into it.

\begin{theorem}[Quantitative defect-thickened strengthened coincidence]
\label{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
Let \((a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)\) be a normalized bad two-pair core, and write
\[
c_i:=c(h_i),
\qquad
A_{5,i}^{\mathfrak f}:=A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h_i)=u_{5,i}I+v_{5,i}S,
\qquad

\]

\[
a_1\neq 0,
\qquad
c_1c_2\neq 0.
\]
Suppose the cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects are written as
\[
a_1c_1+a_2c_2+E_{12}^{(3)}=0,
\]
\[
a_1A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}+a_2A_{5,2}^{\mathfrak f}+E_{12}^{(5)}=0,
\]
and
\[
a_1[A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}]+a_2[A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}]
+\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=0
\qquad\text{in}\qquad
\mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Set
\[
\lambda:=-\frac{a_2}{a_1},
\qquad
e:=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},
\qquad
E:=\frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}=e_u I+e_v S.
\]
Choose any representative \(R\in\mathfrak f\) of the quotient class
\[
-\frac{1}{a_1}\,\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)},
\]
so that
\[
A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}
+
R
+
\eta A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}
\]
for some \(\eta\in\mathbf C\). Then the strengthened invariant
\[
\widehat\Psi(h)=
\left(
\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},
\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)^2}
\right)
\]
satisfies the exact identities
\[
\frac{u_{5,1}}{c_1}-\frac{u_{5,2}}{c_2}
=
\frac{u_{5,2}e-c_2e_u}{c_1c_2},
\]
\[
\frac{v_{5,1}}{c_1}-\frac{v_{5,2}}{c_2}
=
\frac{v_{5,2}e-c_2e_v}{c_1c_2},
\]
and
\[
\frac{\Delta_1}{c_1^2}-\frac{\Delta_2}{c_2^2}
=
\frac{
-\lambda c_2^2\det(A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f},E)
+
c_2^2\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})
+
\Delta_2(2\lambda c_2 e-e^2)
}{c_1^2c_2^2}.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The cubic defect identity gives
\[
c_1=\lambda c_2-e.
\]
The quintic defect identity gives
\[
A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda A_{5,2}^{\mathfrak f}-E,
\]
hence
\[
u_{5,1}=\lambda u_{5,2}-e_u,
\qquad
v_{5,1}=\lambda v_{5,2}-e_v.
\]
Therefore
\[
\frac{u_{5,1}}{c_1}-\frac{u_{5,2}}{c_2}
=
\frac{u_{5,1}c_2-u_{5,2}c_1}{c_1c_2}
=
\frac{(\lambda u_{5,2}-e_u)c_2-u_{5,2}(\lambda c_2-e)}{c_1c_2}
=
\frac{u_{5,2}e-c_2e_u}{c_1c_2},
\]
and similarly
\[
\frac{v_{5,1}}{c_1}-\frac{v_{5,2}}{c_2}
=
\frac{v_{5,2}e-c_2e_v}{c_1c_2}.
\]

For the third coordinate, by the choice of \(R\) we have
\[
A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f}
=
\lambda A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f}
+
R
+
\eta A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}
\]
for some \(\eta\in\mathbf C\). Using
\[
\Delta_i=\det(A_{7,i}^{\mathfrak f},A_{5,i}^{\mathfrak f}),
\]
we obtain
\[
\Delta_1
=
\det(A_{7,1}^{\mathfrak f},A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})
=
\lambda\det(A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f},A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})
+
\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}),
\]
since the \(\eta A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}\) term drops out. Substituting
\[
A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}=\lambda A_{5,2}^{\mathfrak f}-E
\]
gives
\[
\det(A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f},A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})
=
\lambda\Delta_2-\det(A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f},E),
\]
hence
\[
\Delta_1-\lambda^2\Delta_2
=
-\lambda\det(A_{7,2}^{\mathfrak f},E)
+
\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}).
\]

Also,
\[
c_1=\lambda c_2-e
\]
implies
\[
\lambda^2c_2^2-c_1^2=2\lambda c_2 e-e^2.
\]
Therefore
\[
\frac{\Delta_1}{c_1^2}-\frac{\Delta_2}{c_2^2}
=
\frac{c_2^2\Delta_1-c_1^2\Delta_2}{c_1^2c_2^2}
=
\frac{
c_2^2(\Delta_1-\lambda^2\Delta_2)+\Delta_2(\lambda^2c_2^2-c_1^2)
}{c_1^2c_2^2},
\]
which is exactly the claimed formula.

Finally, the expression
\[
\det(R,A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f})
\]
is independent of the chosen representative of the quotient defect, since
replacing \(R\) by \(R+\xi A_{5,1}^{\mathfrak f}\) does not change the
determinant.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Bad two-pair cores are defect-scale close on good \(M\neq 0\) patches]
\label{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}
Let \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be a compact interval. Assume
\[
|a_1|\ge a_*>0
\]
for the normalized bad two-pair core under consideration. Then there exists a
constant \(C_J>0\) such that whenever \(h_1,h_2\in J\),
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\le
C_J\Bigl(|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|\Bigr).
\]
In particular, on good \(M\neq 0\) patches, bad two-pair cores force the two
parameters to be quantitatively close once the cubic/quintic interaction
defects are small.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The second coordinate of \(\widehat\Psi\) is
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}.
\]
Since \(J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\), there exists \(\eta_J>0\) such that
\[
|x(h_1)-x(h_2)|\ge \eta_J\,|h_1-h_2|
\qquad
(h_1,h_2\in J).
\]
On the other hand, Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
gives the exact identity
\[
x(h_1)-x(h_2)
=
\frac{v_{5,2}e-c_2e_v}{c_1c_2},
\]
with
\[
e=\frac{E_{12}^{(3)}}{a_1},
\qquad
e_v=\text{\(S\)-coefficient of } \frac{E_{12}^{(5)}}{a_1}.
\]
Since \(J\) is compact and \(a_1\) is bounded away from \(0\), the right-hand
side is bounded by
\[
C'_J\Bigl(|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|\Bigr)
\]
for some constant \(C'_J\). Combining the two estimates yields the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the correct algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the
strengthened invariant \(\widehat\Psi\). In particular, on good \(M\neq 0\)
patches, bad two-pair cores are forced into a defect-scale close regime by
Corollary~\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}.

What remains is to rewrite the actual interaction germ \(\mathcal I_{12}\)
explicitly in the corrected finite-order model and control the defect terms
\[
E_{12}^{(3)},
\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)},
\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}.
\]
Once that is done, the finite-core endgame splits cleanly into two stages:
first force bad cores into the close-point regime through
\(\widehat\Psi\), then attack that local regime using the lifted \(v_5\)-patch
geometry and the determinants \(K_v\) and \(T_v\).
\end{remark}

This is the strongest thing I think is immediately theorem-ready.

Find this block:

Immediately after it, insert this:

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]
\label{rem:wip-stratified-lifted-local-picture}
The lifted local obstruction now appears to split into three regimes.

First, finite-order isolated zeros of \(K_v\) should be locally sterile for
lifted \(3\)-point birth on \(v_5\neq 0\) patches, by the same
first-contact / divided-difference mechanism as in the finite-order
\(W=0\) theorem.

Second, finite-order isolated zeros of \(T_v\) with \(K_v\neq 0\) should be
locally sterile for lifted \(4\)-point birth, since on such patches the lower
triple
\[
1,\qquad \frac{v_5}{c},\qquad \frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}
\]
is already an ECT system and the order-\(4\) problem reduces to the next
disconjugate layer.

Third, the mixed case
\[
K_v=T_v=0
\]
is genuinely different. After affine normalization with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
as local coordinate, the lifted space curve is led to a monomial model
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\]
and the leading \(4\)-point coplanarity determinant becomes the generalized
Vandermonde for exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
\]
For some exponent patterns this model does admit opposite-side quadruples, so
no blanket mixed local-sterility theorem should be expected.

Thus the remaining lifted local obstruction is concentrated in the mixed
codimension-two case, together with possible infinite-order flatness and the
global recurrence / re-entry problem.
\end{remark}

This is the cleanest way to get the new structural lesson into the draft without overclaiming.

Here’s the cleanest way I see to continue the attack.

The first thing to say is that the picture has sharpened enough that we should now **separate the endgame by core size**. The two-point route and the lifted (3/4)-point route are related, but they are not the same obstruction.

For a **two-point** bad core, the new quantitative theorem for
[
\widehat\Psi(h)=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)^2}\right)
]
is the main tool: it forces near-coincidence of (\widehat\Psi(h_1)) and (\widehat\Psi(h_2)). On a good patch with (c\neq 0) and (M\neq 0), the second coordinate
[

]
has derivative
[

[

\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+|E_{12}^{(5)}|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|.
]
That is already real progress.

If we can prove on good patches that the interaction defects are actually **superlinear** in the separation,
[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+|E_{12}^{(5)}|+|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}|
========================================================

o(|h_1-h_2|),
]
or even better
[
O(|h_1-h_2|^2),
]
then two-point bad cores are impossible on such patches.

The proof would be simple. Write
[
\widehat\Psi(h_2)-\widehat\Psi(h_1)
===================================

(h_2-h_1)\widehat\Psi'(h_1)+O(|h_2-h_1|^2).
]
Since the second coordinate derivative is
[
\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}\neq 0,
]
we have (\widehat\Psi'(h_1)\neq 0). So if the right-hand side from the defect theorem were (o(|h_2-h_1|)), the only possibility would be (h_2=h_1). In other words:

> **Sufficient next theorem for the two-point branch:**
> prove the interaction defects are superlinear in pair separation on good patches.

That would kill the entire two-point bad-core regime away from patch boundaries. This is now the sharpest next algebraic target. 

Now for **three- and four-point minimal bad cores**, the correct local objects are the lifted determinants (K_v) and (T_v). The other chat’s summary makes the stratification very clear:

* finite-order isolated (K_v=0) is locally sterile for lifted (3)-point birth;
* finite-order isolated (T_v=0) with (K_v\neq 0) is locally sterile for lifted (4)-point birth;
* the mixed codimension-two locus
  [
  K_v=T_v=0
  ]
  is the one local case not killed by the blanket sterility mechanism, because its monomial normal form can have a generalized-Vandermonde vanishing. 

So the continuation there is:

> **Local exclusion away from the mixed locus:**
> prove that on a (v_5\neq 0) patch, close-point bad (3)-point or (4)-point affine circuits cannot accumulate at a point where either (K_v\neq 0), or (T_v\neq 0), or (T_v=0) but (K_v\neq 0) with finite order.

That would immediately imply a concentration theorem:

> any small-defect bad finite core on a good patch can accumulate only at the mixed lifted locus (K_v=T_v=0), or at patch boundaries / turning boundaries.

So the attack sequence now looks like this:

First, finish the **two-point algebraic branch** by proving a superlinear defect estimate. That is the cleanest next theorem.

Second, formalize the **local close-point exclusion** for the lifted (3/4)-point branches away from (K_v=T_v=0). This uses the sterility theorems the other chat outlined. 

Third, conclude the concentration theorem:
bad finite cores with small defects can only survive near the mixed lifted locus (or other non-good boundaries).

So the route has become much sharper:

* **two-point cores** are now mainly an **interaction-defect order** problem;
* **three/four-point cores** are now mainly a **lifted mixed-locus** problem.

That is a much better split than before.

Insert this block:

\begin{proposition}[No sublinear two-pair defects on good patches]
\label{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch}
Let
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}
\]
be a compact interval. Then there exists a constant \(C_J>0\) such that every
normalized bad two-pair core with \(h_1,h_2\in J\) and \(h_1\neq h_2\)
satisfies
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
\ge
C_J^{-1}\,|h_1-h_2|.
\]
In particular, there is no sequence of nontrivial normalized bad two-pair
cores in \(J\) for which
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
o\!\left(|h_1-h_2|\right).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}, there exists a
constant \(C'_J>0\) such that
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\le
C'_J\Bigl(|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|\Bigr)
\]
for every normalized bad two-pair core with \(h_1,h_2\in J\). Since
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|
\le
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|,
\]
the same estimate yields
\[
|h_1-h_2|
\le
C'_J\Bigl(
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
\Bigr).
\]
Renaming \(C'_J\) as \(C_J\) proves the first claim. The final statement is
immediate: if a sequence satisfied
\[
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
o\!\left(|h_1-h_2|\right),
\]
then the displayed lower bound would force
\[
|h_1-h_2|=o\!\left(|h_1-h_2|\right),
\]
which is impossible for a nontrivial two-point core with \(h_1\neq h_2\).
\end{proof}

A very small optional follow-up edit: in the remark right after it, you could change

bad two-pair cores are forced into a defect-scale close regime

to

bad two-pair cores are forced into a defect-scale close regime, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch} shows that the
two-point branch is already excluded whenever the total defect is sublinear in
the pair separation

If you want that exact replacement sentence too, use:

Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
supplies the correct algebraic bridge from the two-pair core to the
strengthened invariant \(\widehat\Psi\). In particular, on good \(M\neq 0\)
patches, bad two-pair cores are forced into a defect-scale close regime by
Corollary~\ref{cor:bad-two-pair-cores-defect-scale-close}, and
Proposition~\ref{prop:no-sublinear-two-pair-defects-good-patch} shows that the
two-point branch is already excluded whenever the total defect is sublinear in
the pair separation.

Yes. The clean bridge you can add mathematically, right now, is a repeated-node/tangent-contact bridge. It does not finish the full concentration theorem, but it gives the exact missing local translation from “two nearby support points” to the lifted Kv/TvKv​/Tv​ geometry.

Here is the right setup on a good v5v5​-patch:
x=v5c,Y=u5c,S=σv=Δ7cv5,
x=cv5​​,Y=cu5​​,S=σv​=cv5​Δ7​​,

so
Λv=(x,S),Qv=(Y,x,S).
Λv​=(x,S),Qv​=(Y,x,S).

Because M≠0M=0, xx is a valid local coordinate.
1. The exact repeated-node bridge for the 3-point lifted branch

Define the collinearity determinant
Δ3(a,b,u):=det⁡ ⁣(1aS(a)1bS(b)1uS(u)).
Δ3​(a,b,u):=det
​111​abu​S(a)S(b)S(u)​
​.

Then
Δ3(a,b,u)b−a⟶det⁡ ⁣(1aS(a)01S′(a)1uS(u))(b→a).
b−aΔ3​(a,b,u)​⟶det
​101​a1u​S(a)S′(a)S(u)​
​(b→a).

That is just differentiating the second row with respect to bb. The limiting determinant says exactly:

    if a secant through (a,S(a))(a,S(a)) and (b,S(b))(b,S(b)) persists as b→ab→a, then the limit point (u,S(u))(u,S(u)) lies on the tangent line to ΛvΛv​ at aa.

So the rigorous bridge is:

    a shrinking exact lifted 3-point circuit does not just “go near Kv=0Kv​=0”;

    if only one pair collapses, it limits to a tangent-line contact configuration for ΛvΛv​;

    if all three points collapse, then the divided-difference limit gives Kv(a)=0Kv​(a)=0.

So there are really two close-point regimes for 3-point circuits:
tangent-line contact with one repeated node, and full triple collapse to Kv=0Kv​=0.
2. The exact repeated-node bridge for the 4-point lifted branch

Define the coplanarity determinant
Δ4(a,b,u,v):=det⁡ ⁣(1Y(a)aS(a)1Y(b)bS(b)1Y(u)uS(u)1Y(v)vS(v)).
Δ4​(a,b,u,v):=det
​1111​Y(a)Y(b)Y(u)Y(v)​abuv​S(a)S(b)S(u)S(v)​
​.

Then
Δ4(a,b,u,v)b−a⟶det⁡ ⁣(1Y(a)aS(a)0Y′(a)1S′(a)1Y(u)uS(u)1Y(v)vS(v))(b→a).
b−aΔ4​(a,b,u,v)​⟶det
​1011​Y(a)Y′(a)Y(u)Y(v)​a1uv​S(a)S′(a)S(u)S(v)​
​(b→a).

Again this is just the row-derivative limit. The limiting determinant says:

    if a coplanar quadruple has one pair collapsing, then the two surviving points and the collapsing point lie in the tangent plane to QvQv​ at the collision point.

So for the 4-point branch the exact bridge is:

    one collapsing pair gives a tangent-plane contact configuration for QvQv​;

    full quadruple collapse gives Tv(a)=0Tv​(a)=0 by the divided-difference/Wronskian limit.

3. Why this is the right missing bridge

This is exactly what was missing in the informal concentration-to-Kv=Tv=0Kv​=Tv​=0 claim.

The sterility theorems you already have are about local birth of collinear/coplanar configurations across KvKv​- or TvTv​-boundaries.

What was not yet written was the passage from a close support pair to those local geometric objects.

These two determinant limits give that passage exactly:

    nearby support points produce tangent-line or tangent-plane contact in the lifted geometry;

    total collapse produces Kv=0Kv​=0 or Tv=0Tv​=0.

So the real local obstruction away from the mixed locus is not just “close points.” It is:

    tangent-line contact for ΛvΛv​,

    tangent-plane contact for QvQv​,

    or full collapse to Kv=0Kv​=0 or Tv=0Tv​=0.

4. What this proves immediately

It proves a clean intermediate theorem for exact lifted circuits:

On a good v5v5​-patch, any shrinking sequence of exact lifted 3-point circuits has a subsequence converging either to:

    a tangent-line contact configuration for ΛvΛv​, or

    a full collapse point with Kv=0Kv​=0.

Likewise, any shrinking sequence of exact lifted 4-point circuits has a subsequence converging either to:

    a tangent-plane contact configuration for QvQv​, or

    a full collapse point with Tv=0Tv​=0.

That is rigorous now.
5. What still remains for the full concentration theorem

The remaining gap is now much narrower:

You still need to show that, on a good patch away from the mixed locus and away from any explicit exceptional coincidence set, these tangent-line/tangent-plane contact configurations cannot persist.

So the full concentration theorem is not yet:
close bad cores⟹Kv=Tv=0.
close bad cores⟹Kv​=Tv​=0.

What you do have is:
close bad cores⟹tangent contact or full collapse in the lifted geometry.
close bad cores⟹tangent contact or full collapse in the lifted geometry.

That is the right bridge.
6. How I would split the next math

There are now two separate next tasks.

For the two-point branch, the clean next target is still the superlinear defect estimate:
∣E12(3)∣+∥E12(5)∥+∣E‾12(7;1)∣=o(∣h1−h2∣),
∣E12(3)​∣+∥E12(5)​∥+∣E12(7;1)​∣=o(∣h1​−h2​∣),

or ideally O(∣h1−h2∣2)O(∣h1​−h2​∣2). If that holds, the two-point branch dies immediately on good patches.

For the 3/4-point branch, the clean next target is:
prove that on a good v5v5​-patch away from the mixed locus, the tangent-line and tangent-plane contact limits above are locally sterile.

That is now a sharply formulated local theorem, not a vague bridge.

So yes — this is the bridge I can add right now: collapsing pairs become repeated-node tangent-contact determinants in the lifted geometry. That is the exact local translation that was missing.

3. What this proves now

It proves a genuine intermediate theorem:

On a compact good v5v5​-patch, any shrinking exact lifted 3-point circuit has accumulation points only in Kv=0Kv​=0, and any shrinking exact lifted 4-point circuit has accumulation points only in Tv=0Tv​=0.

More sharply:

    away from Kv=0Kv​=0, there is a uniform diagonal collar with no tangent-line contacts and hence no shrinking 3-point circuits;

    away from Tv=0Tv​=0, there is a uniform diagonal collar with no tangent-plane contacts and hence no shrinking 4-point circuits with one collapsing pair.

And combining this with the finite-order sterility theorems gives:

    shrinking 3-point lifted obstructions can only persist at infinite-order flatness of KvKv​;

    shrinking 4-point lifted obstructions can only persist at infinite-order flatness of TvTv​ or at the mixed locus
    Kv=Tv=0.
    Kv​=Tv​=0.

That is now a real theorem-level reduction.

(h2​), but not yet an exact lifted 3-point or 4-point circuit. So one still needs a separate argument to turn a collapsing pair in a bad core into one of these repeated-node tangent-contact patterns, or else kill the two-point branch directly by a superlinear defect estimate.

shrinking configurations limit to tangent-line or tangent-plane contacts, and those are uniformly excluded away from Kv=0Kv​=0 and Tv=0Tv​=0.

The key point is exactly the one the other chat found: a blanket theorem of the form “near a finite-order nonmixed zero, there cannot be a preexisting close lifted branch” is false in generic lifted geometry. The examples

for the 33-point branch and

    shrinking exact lifted 33-point circuits can only accumulate at Kv=0Kv​=0;

    If the raw corrected two-pair interaction germ is quadratic in amplitudes, symmetric under pair swap, and collapses to zero on the diagonal, then the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches.

Now the important caveat:

F(a1,h;a2,h)=(a1+a2)Fh.
F(a1​,h;a2​,h)​=(a1​+a2​)Fh​.

If that identity is literally true for the raw corrected finite-order object you are decomposing, then the argument above goes through.

Now, which of the three is delicate?

Quadratic onset is usually the easiest. If II is defined as “full two-pair corrected object minus the two one-pair corrected objects,” then setting a1=0a1​=0 or a2=0a2​=0 collapses it to a one-pair object, so the remainder should vanish. That gives the a1a2a1​a2​ factor.

Swap symmetry should also be built in, provided the raw corrected two-pair object is defined before any asymmetric normalization by a1a1​. The unordered pair {(a1,h1),(a2,h2)}{(a1​,h1​),(a2​,h2​)} should not depend on the labeling. So this should give

I(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=I(a2​,h2​;a1​,h1​).

The truly important one is diagonal collapse:
F(a1,h;a2,h)=F1(a1+a2,h).
F(a1​,h;a2​,h)=F1​(a1​+a2​,h).

If that identity is literally true for the corrected object you are decomposing, then the two-point branch is basically finished.

Here is the clean verdict.

The current draft gives you this and only this at the two-pair structural level:

I12=a1a2(h1−h2)2J.
I12​=a1​a2​(h1​−h2​)2J.

Why not?

Because the three exact properties needed for that factorization are not yet present as theorem-level statements.

The three properties are:
(A) swap symmetry:   I(a1,h1;a2,h2)=I(a2,h2;a1,h1),
(A) swap symmetry: I(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=I(a2​,h2​;a1​,h1​),
(B) one-pair collapse:   I(0,h1;a2,h2)=I(a1,h1;0,h2)=0,
(B) one-pair collapse: I(0,h1​;a2​,h2​)=I(a1​,h1​;0,h2​)=0,
(C) diagonal collapse:   F(a1,h;a2,h)=F1(a1+a2,h),
(C) diagonal collapse: F(a1​,h;a2​,h)=F1​(a1​+a2​,h),

equivalently
I(a1,h;a2,h)=0.
I(a1​,h;a2​,h)=0.

Here is the status of each one in the current draft.
1. Swap symmetry: plausible, but not stated

The notation and the mathematics strongly suggest that a two-pair core should not depend on the ordering of the two labels. So morally
F(a1,h1;a2,h2)=F(a2,h2;a1,h1)
F(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)​=F(a2​,h2​;a1​,h1​)​

should be true, and then I12I12​ would inherit the same symmetry.

But the draft does not currently state this explicitly. The definition uses an ordered tuple notation (a1,h1;a2,h2)(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​), and nowhere in the section is there a proposition saying the resulting quotient odd germ is invariant under swapping the two labels.

So:

    likely true by intention

    not yet a theorem / not yet available for proof

2. One-pair collapse when one amplitude is zero: not available

This is the crucial subtlety.

The draft says I12I12​ is “quadratic in the pair amplitudes,” but that alone is too weak. A general quadratic function of (a1,a2)(a1​,a2​) can contain terms like
a12,a22,a1a2.
a12​,a22​,a1​a2​.

To conclude divisibility by a1a2a1​a2​, you need
I(0,h1;a2,h2)=0andI(a1,h1;0,h2)=0.
I(0,h1​;a2​,h2​)=0andI(a1​,h1​;0,h2​)=0.

The current draft does not state this.

So right now, the paper does not justify the step
I12=a1a2 G(h1,h2;z).
I12​=a1​a2​G(h1​,h2​;z).

That step is essential.
3. Diagonal collapse h1=h2h1​=h2​: not available

This is the real hinge.

To get the (h1−h2)2(h1​−h2​)2 factor, you need the identity
F(a1,h;a2,h)=F1(a1+a2,h),
F(a1​,h;a2​,h)=F1​(a1​+a2​,h),

so that after subtracting the two one-pair pieces, the raw interaction remainder vanishes on the diagonal:
I(a1,h;a2,h)=0.
I(a1​,h;a2​,h)=0.

The current draft does not state this anywhere.

Nothing in the present “Two-pair decomposition” definition or the later quantitative defect theorem records diagonal collapse for the raw corrected two-pair object.

So at the moment, the core quadratic-separation factor
(h1−h2)2
(h1​−h2​)2

is not justified from the paper.
4. The normalized defects are the wrong level to test symmetry

This matters a lot.

The paper’s theorem is written in terms of
E12(3),E12(5),E‾12(7;1),
E12(3)​,E12(5)​,E12(7;1)​,

after normalization by a1a1​ and after passing to the quotient/septic representative bookkeeping.

That is not the right level to test evenness in the separation variable. Dividing by a1a1​ destroys the visible symmetry under swapping the two pair labels. So even if the raw interaction remainder is symmetric/even in separation, the normalized defects will not show that directly.

So the test must happen one layer earlier:

    define the raw unnormalized cubic/quintic/septic interaction defects,

    prove those are symmetric under pair swap,

    prove they vanish when one amplitude is zero,

    prove they vanish on the diagonal h1=h2h1​=h2​,

    then conclude O((h1−h2)2)O((h1​−h2​)2),

    only then divide by a1a1​.

That is the correct order.
So where does this leave the attack?

Yes. Here is the clean rigorous math formulation.

I would package it as a conditional source-level theorem. If you can make these assumptions true for the corrected quotient-germ map actually used in the paper, then the two-point branch is finished on good patches.
1. Source-level setup

Fix the corrected quotient-germ target through order 77; call it GG. You do not need to identify GG further for this argument, only that:

    GG is a finite-dimensional complex vector space,

    the cubic, quintic, and septic quotient data are extracted by linear maps
    Π3:G→C,Π5:G→f,Πˉ7:G→f/CA5f.
    Π3​:G→C,Π5​:G→f,Πˉ7​:G→f/CA5f​.

Now introduce a raw corrected quotient-germ map
Q:μ⟼Q(μ)∈G
Q:μ⟼Q(μ)∈G

defined for small finite atomic sources
μ=∑jajδhj.
μ=j∑​aj​δhj​​.

For the two-point branch, you only need it on one- and two-atom sources:
F1(a,h):=Q(aδh),F2(a1,h1;a2,h2):=Q(a1δh1+a2δh2).
F1​(a,h):=Q(aδh​),F2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​):=Q(a1​δh1​​+a2​δh2​​).

Define the raw interaction remainder
I(a1,h1;a2,h2):=F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)−F1(a1,h1)−F1(a2,h2).
I(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​):=F2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)−F1​(a1​,h1​)−F1​(a2​,h2​).
2. Structural assumptions needed

The whole argument rests on these four assumptions.
(S1) Analyticity

The map (a1,h1,a2,h2)↦F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)(a1​,h1​,a2​,h2​)↦F2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​) is analytic, and likewise (a,h)↦F1(a,h)(a,h)↦F1​(a,h) is analytic.
(S2) Source symmetry
F2(a1,h1;a2,h2)=F2(a2,h2;a1,h1).
F2​(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=F2​(a2​,h2​;a1​,h1​).

Equivalently, QQ depends only on the atomic source
a1δh1+a2δh2,
a1​δh1​​+a2​δh2​​,

not on the ordering of the two atoms.
(S3) One-pair collapse
F2(0,h1;a2,h2)=F1(a2,h2),F2(a1,h1;0,h2)=F1(a1,h1).
F2​(0,h1​;a2​,h2​)=F1​(a2​,h2​),F2​(a1​,h1​;0,h2​)=F1​(a1​,h1​).

Equivalently,
I(0,h1;a2,h2)=I(a1,h1;0,h2)=0.
I(0,h1​;a2​,h2​)=I(a1​,h1​;0,h2​)=0.
(S4) Diagonal collapse
F2(a1,h;a2,h)=F1(a1+a2,h).
F2​(a1​,h;a2​,h)=F1​(a1​+a2​,h).

Equivalently,
I(a1,h;a2,h)=0.
I(a1​,h;a2​,h)=0.

This is the crucial one.
3. Structural factorization theorem

Under (S1)–(S4), the raw interaction remainder has the exact factorization
I(a1,h1;a2,h2)=a1a2(h1−h2)2 J(a1,h1;a2,h2)
I(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=a1​a2​(h1​−h2​)2J(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)​

for some analytic JJ with values in GG.
Proof

From (S3), II vanishes when a1=0a1​=0 or a2=0a2​=0. By analyticity, it is divisible by a1a2a1​a2​:
I(a1,h1;a2,h2)=a1a2 G(h1,h2)
I(a1​,h1​;a2​,h2​)=a1​a2​G(h1​,h2​)

for some analytic GG valued in GG.

From (S2), GG is symmetric:
G(h1,h2)=G(h2,h1).
G(h1​,h2​)=G(h2​,h1​).

From (S4),
G(h,h)=0.
G(h,h)=0.

Now pass to midpoint/separation variables
m=h1+h22,s=h2−h1.
m=2h1​+h2​​,s=h2​−h1​.

Set
G~(m,s):=G ⁣(m−s2,m+s2).
G
(m,s):=G(m−2s​,m+2s​).

Symmetry gives
G~(m,s)=G~(m,−s),
G
(m,s)=G
(m,−s),

so G~G
is even in ss. Since G(h,h)=0G(h,h)=0, we have
G~(m,0)=0.
G
(m,0)=0.

Thus G~G
has no constant term in its Taylor expansion in ss, and since it is even, it has no linear term either. Therefore
G~(m,s)=s2H(m,s)
G
(m,s)=s2H(m,s)

for analytic HH. Returning to (h1,h2)(h1​,h2​) gives
G(h1,h2)=(h1−h2)2 J(h1,h2)
G(h1​,h2​)=(h1​−h2​)2J(h1​,h2​)

for analytic JJ, hence the claimed factorization.
4. Raw coefficient defects are quadratic in separation

Define the raw cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects by linear projection:
E(3):=Π3(I),E(5):=Π5(I),E‾(7):=Πˉ7(I).
E(3):=Π3​(I),E(5):=Π5​(I),E(7):=Πˉ7​(I).

Since Π3,Π5,Πˉ7Π3​,Π5​,Πˉ7​ are linear, the factorization immediately implies
E(3)=a1a2 O(δ2),E(5)=a1a2 O(δ2),E‾(7)=a1a2 O(δ2)
E(3)=a1​a2​O(δ2),E(5)=a1​a2​O(δ2),E(7)=a1​a2​O(δ2)​

uniformly on compacta, where
δ:=∣h1−h2∣.

5. Passing to the paper’s normalized defects

namely
∣Ψ^(h1)−Ψ^(h2)∣≤C(∣E12(3)∣+∥E12(5)∥+∣E‾12(7;1)∣)
∣Ψ
(h1​)−Ψ
(h2​)∣≤C(∣E12(3)​∣+∥E12(5)​∥+∣E12(7;1)​∣)

on compact good patches.

Let

be compact. Then

satisfies

so xx is bi-Lipschitz on JJ. Therefore there is ηJ>0ηJ​>0 such that

So the final theorem is:

    Two-point exclusion theorem.
    Under (S1)–(S4), the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches.

7. What remains to verify in the actual paper

This is now the exact checklist.

You do not need to prove O(δ2)O(δ2) directly. You only need to verify that the current corrected construction actually comes from a source-level map QQ with (S1)–(S4).

Concretely:

    Is the current corrected two-pair object literally
    Q(a1δh1+a2δh2)?
    Q(a1​δh1​​+a2​δh2​​)?

    Is the current corrected one-pair object literally
    Q(aδh)?
    Q(aδh​)?

    Does the current decomposition define the raw interaction remainder by subtraction of the two one-pair corrected objects?

If yes, then:

    source symmetry is automatic;

    one-pair collapse is automatic;

    diagonal collapse is automatic.

And the two-point branch is done.
8. The main caveat

This whole theorem is about the raw unnormalized interaction remainder.

It is not enough to look at the already normalized defects
E12(3),E12(5),E‾12(7;1),
E12(3)​,E12(5)​,E12(7;1)​,

because dividing by a1a1​ breaks the symmetry under swapping the two labels. The symmetry argument belongs one level earlier, before normalization.
Bottom line

The rigorous math is now:

    If the corrected construction is source-level and additive on coincident atoms, then the raw two-pair interaction remainder is automatically
    a1a2(h1−h2)2×(analytic).
    a1​a2​(h1​−h2​)2×(analytic).

    Therefore the normalized defects are O(∣h1−h2∣2)O(∣h1​−h2​∣2).

    Therefore the two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.

So the next actual task is not more asymptotic analysis. It is to check whether the present paper’s corrected object is already defined source-level enough for (S2)–(S4) to be formal.

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]

Use this:

\begin{proposition}[Conditional source-level quadratic interaction remainder]
\label{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
Assume there exists a finite-dimensional corrected quotient-germ target
\(\mathcal G\) and an analytic map
\[
\mathfrak Q:\mu\longmapsto \mathfrak Q(\mu)\in\mathcal G
\]
defined on small finite atomic sources
\[
\mu=\sum_j a_j\delta_{h_j},
\]
such that the corrected one-pair and two-pair objects are given by
\[
\mathcal F_1(a,h):=\mathfrak Q(a\,\delta_h),
\qquad
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2):=\mathfrak Q(a_1\delta_{h_1}+a_2\delta_{h_2}).
\]
Define the raw interaction remainder by
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
:=
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
-\mathcal F_1(a_1,h_1)-\mathcal F_1(a_2,h_2).
\]
Then there exists an analytic germ-valued map \(\mathcal J\) such that
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)
=
a_1a_2\,(h_1-h_2)^2\,\mathcal J(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2).
}
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The source-level definition of \(\mathcal F_2\) is symmetric in the two atoms,
so
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_2,h_2;a_1,h_1).
\]
Also, if one amplitude is zero, then the two-pair source reduces to a one-pair
source, hence
\[
\mathcal I(0,h_1;a_2,h_2)=\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;0,h_2)=0.
\]
Thus \(\mathcal I\) is divisible by \(a_1a_2\), so
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h_1;a_2,h_2)=a_1a_2\,G(h_1,h_2)
\]
for some analytic \(\mathcal G\)-valued map \(G\).

Now if \(h_1=h_2=h\), then
\[
a_1\delta_h+a_2\delta_h=(a_1+a_2)\delta_h,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal F_2(a_1,h;a_2,h)=\mathcal F_1(a_1+a_2,h),
\]
and therefore
\[
\mathcal I(a_1,h;a_2,h)=0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
G(h,h)=0.
\]

Passing to midpoint/separation variables
\[
m=\frac{h_1+h_2}{2},
\qquad
s=h_2-h_1,
\]
the symmetry of \(G\) means that
\[
\widetilde G(m,s):=G\!\left(m-\frac s2,m+\frac s2\right)
\]
is an even analytic function of \(s\), and the diagonal vanishing gives
\[
\widetilde G(m,0)=0.
\]
Hence \(\widetilde G(m,s)\) is divisible by \(s^2\):
\[
\widetilde G(m,s)=s^2 H(m,s)
\]
for analytic \(H\). Rewriting in \((h_1,h_2)\) gives the claimed
factorization.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Conditional quadratic defect estimate and two-point exclusion]
\label{cor:conditional-quadratic-defect-estimate-two-point-exclusion}
Assume, in addition to
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder},
that the raw cubic, quintic, and septic quotient defects are obtained from the
raw interaction remainder by linear coefficient-extraction maps
\[
\Pi_3:\mathcal G\to\mathbf C,
\qquad
\Pi_5:\mathcal G\to\mathfrak f,
\qquad
\bar\Pi_7:\mathcal G\to \mathfrak f/\mathbf C A_5^{\mathfrak f}.
\]
Then on compacta, the raw defects satisfy
\[
\mathcal E^{(3)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\mathcal E^{(5)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline{\mathcal E}^{(7)}=a_1a_2\,O(\delta^2),
\qquad
\delta:=|h_1-h_2|.
\]
If the normalized defects in the present two-pair section are obtained by
dividing by \(a_1\), then on normalized families with \(|a_2|\) bounded one has
\[
E_{12}^{(3)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
E_{12}^{(5)}=O(\delta^2),\qquad
\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}=O(\delta^2).
\]
Consequently, the two-point bad-core branch is excluded on compact good patches
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The first claim is immediate from the factorization in
Proposition~\ref{prop:conditional-source-level-quadratic-interaction-remainder}
and the linearity of the coefficient-extraction maps.

For the normalized defects, divide by \(a_1\) and use boundedness of \(|a_2|\)
on normalized families. Then
Theorem~\ref{thm:quantitative-defect-thickened-strengthened-coincidence}
gives
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|
\lesssim
|E_{12}^{(3)}|+\|E_{12}^{(5)}\|+\bigl|\overline E_{12}^{(7;1)}\bigr|
=
O(\delta^2).
\]
On the other hand, on every compact good patch
\[
J\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
the second coordinate
\[
x(h)=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}
\]
is bi-Lipschitz, since
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2}\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
|\widehat\Psi(h_1)-\widehat\Psi(h_2)|\gtrsim \delta.
\]
Combining the two inequalities gives
\[
\delta\lesssim \delta^2,
\]
which is impossible for sufficiently small nonzero \(\delta\). Thus the
two-point branch is excluded on compact good patches.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: source-level reduction for the two-point branch]
\label{rem:wip-source-level-reduction-two-point-branch}
The preceding proposition and corollary isolate the exact structural input
needed to finish the two-point branch. At present, the draft does not yet define
a source-level corrected quotient-germ map \(\mathfrak Q\) on finite atomic
sources, so the factorization
\[
\mathcal I=a_1a_2(h_1-h_2)^2\mathcal J
\]
is not yet available formally from the present definitions. If such a
source-level reformulation is supplied, then the two-point bad-core branch is
finished on compact good patches.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[What remains in the two-pair rewrite]
\label{rem:what-remains-two-pair-rewrite}

Use this:

\begin{proposition}[Shrinking exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into \(K_v=0\)]
\label{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}
Let \(P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact, and use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Suppose there is a sequence of distinct triples
\[
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\in x(P),
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\to x_*,
\]
such that
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_{1,n}&S(x_{1,n})\\
1&x_{2,n}&S(x_{2,n})\\
1&x_{3,n}&S(x_{3,n})
\end{pmatrix}
=0
\qquad
\text{for every }n.
\]
Then
\[
K_v(x_*)=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&x_3&S(x_3)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
By the standard divided-difference factorization,
\[
\Delta_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)
=
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3)\,S[x_1,x_2,x_3],
\]
where
\[
V_3(x_1,x_2,x_3):=(x_2-x_1)(x_3-x_1)(x_3-x_2).
\]
Since the nodes are distinct, \(V_3(x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n})\neq 0\), so
\[
S[x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}]=0.
\]
As \(x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n}\to x_*\), the second divided difference converges
to
\[
\frac12 S''(x_*).
\]
Hence \(S''(x_*)=0\). Since on the \(x\)-patch the lifted curvature numerator
\(K_v\) is \(S''\) up to a nowhere-zero factor, it follows that \(K_v(x_*)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Uniform small-diameter exclusion away from \(K_v=0\)]
\label{cor:uniform-small-diameter-exclusion-away-from-Kv-zero}
Let \(P_0\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact and assume
\[
P_0\cap\{K_v=0\}=\varnothing.
\]
Then there exists \(\rho_3>0\) such that no exact lifted \(3\)-point circuit
contained in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_3\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Otherwise there would exist a sequence of exact lifted \(3\)-point circuits in
\(P_0\) with diameters tending to \(0\). By compactness, after passing to a
subsequence the three nodes would converge to some \(x_*\in x(P_0)\). This
contradicts
Proposition~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Shrinking exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into \(T_v=0\)]
\label{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero}
Let \(P\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact, and use
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}.
\]
Suppose there is a sequence of distinct quadruples
\[
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n},x_{4,n}\in x(P),
\qquad
x_{1,n},x_{2,n},x_{3,n},x_{4,n}\to x_*,
\]
such that
\[
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(x_{1,n})&x_{1,n}&S(x_{1,n})\\
1&Y(x_{2,n})&x_{2,n}&S(x_{2,n})\\
1&Y(x_{3,n})&x_{3,n}&S(x_{3,n})\\
1&Y(x_{4,n})&x_{4,n}&S(x_{4,n})
\end{pmatrix}
=0
\qquad
\text{for every }n.
\]
Then
\[
T_v(x_*)=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Set
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(x_1)&x_1&S(x_1)\\
1&Y(x_2)&x_2&S(x_2)\\
1&Y(x_3)&x_3&S(x_3)\\
1&Y(x_4)&x_4&S(x_4)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Since \(\Delta_4\) is alternating in the four nodes, it is divisible by the
Vandermonde
\[
V_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4):=\prod_{1\le i<j\le 4}(x_j-x_i).
\]
Write
\[
\Delta_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)
=
V_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\,\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4),
\]
where \(\mathcal D_4\) is symmetric and analytic. By the standard
Wronskian/divided-difference coalescence formula,
\[
\mathcal D_4(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)\longrightarrow
\frac{1}{1!\,2!\,3!}\,W_x(1,Y,x,S)(x_*)
=
\frac1{12}T_v(x_*),
\]
as all four nodes tend to \(x_*\). Since \(V_4\neq 0\) for distinct nodes and
\(\Delta_4=0\) along the sequence, one has \(\mathcal D_4=0\) along the
sequence, so the limit forces \(T_v(x_*)=0\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Uniform small-diameter exclusion away from \(T_v=0\)]
\label{cor:uniform-small-diameter-exclusion-away-from-Tv-zero}
Let \(P_0\Subset\{c\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\}\) be compact and assume
\[
P_0\cap\{T_v=0\}=\varnothing.
\]
Then there exists \(\rho_4>0\) such that no exact lifted \(4\)-point circuit
contained in \(P_0\) has \(x\)-diameter \(<\rho_4\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Otherwise there would exist a sequence of exact lifted \(4\)-point circuits in
\(P_0\) with diameters tending to \(0\). By compactness, after passing to a
subsequence the four nodes would converge to some \(x_*\in x(P_0)\). This
contradicts
Proposition~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero}.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Repeated-node tangent-contact determinants on a \(v_5\)-patch]
\label{def:repeated-node-tangent-contact-determinants-vpatch}
On a \(v_5\neq 0\) patch with \(x=v_5/c\), \(Y=u_5/c\), and
\(S=\Delta_7/(c\,v_5)\), define
\[
H_3(a,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&a&S(a)\\
0&1&S'(a)\\
1&u&S(u)
\end{pmatrix}
=
S(u)-S(a)-S'(a)(u-a),
\]
and
\[
H_4(a,u,v):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(a)&a&S(a)\\
0&Y'(a)&1&S'(a)\\
1&Y(u)&u&S(u)\\
1&Y(v)&v&S(v)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Thus \(H_3(a,u)=0\) means that \((u,S(u))\) lies on the tangent line to
\(\Lambda_v\) at \(a\), while \(H_4(a,u,v)=0\) means that \(Q_v(u)\) and
\(Q_v(v)\) lie in the tangent plane to \(Q_v\) at \(a\).
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Repeated-node limits of exact lifted determinants]
\label{prop:repeated-node-limits-of-exact-lifted-determinants}
For the exact lifted determinants
\[
\Delta_3(a,b,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&a&S(a)\\
1&b&S(b)\\
1&u&S(u)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and
\[
\Delta_4(a,b,u,v):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y(a)&a&S(a)\\
1&Y(b)&b&S(b)\\
1&Y(u)&u&S(u)\\
1&Y(v)&v&S(v)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one has
\[
\frac{\Delta_3(a,b,u)}{b-a}\longrightarrow H_3(a,u)
\qquad (b\to a),
\]
and
\[
\frac{\Delta_4(a,b,u,v)}{b-a}\longrightarrow H_4(a,u,v)
\qquad (b\to a).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Subtract the first row from the second row in each determinant and divide by
\(b-a\). The resulting second row is the first difference quotient of the
corresponding row entries, and the limit \(b\to a\) gives the derivative row.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Local classification of the lifted \(3\)-point branch near a finite-order \(K_v\)-zero]
\label{thm:local-classification-lifted-three-point-branch-near-Kv-zero}
Let \(x=0\) be an isolated finite-order zero of \(K_v\) on a good \(v_5\)-patch.
After affine normalization of \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\), write
\[
S(x)=x^m+O(x^{m+1}),
\qquad
m=r+2\ge 3,
\]
where \(r=\ord_0 K_v\). Then the repeated-node tangent-contact equation
\[
H_3(a,u)=0
\]
with \(a<0<u\) has the following local classification:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(r\) is even (equivalently \(m\) is even), there is no
opposite-side tangent-contact branch near \((a,u)=(0,0)\);
\item if \(r\) is odd (equivalently \(m\) is odd), there exists a unique
real-analytic opposite-side branch
\[
u=\Upsilon(a),
\qquad
a<0,\quad |a|\ll 1,
\]
with asymptotic expansion
\[
\Upsilon(a)=\lambda_m(-a)+O(a^2),
\]
where \(\lambda_m>1\) is the unique positive root of
\[
P_m(\lambda):=\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1).
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Set \(a=-\alpha\) with \(\alpha>0\), and write \(u=\lambda\alpha\) with
\(\lambda>0\). For the model germ \(S(x)=x^m\), the tangent-contact equation is
\[
H_3(-\alpha,\lambda\alpha)
=
\alpha^m
\begin{cases}
\lambda^m+m\lambda+(m-1),& m\ \text{even},\\[0.5ex]
\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1),& m\ \text{odd}.
\end{cases}
\]
If \(m\) is even, the displayed factor is strictly positive for every
\(\lambda>0\), so no opposite-side branch exists.

If \(m\) is odd, define
\[
P_m(\lambda):=\lambda^m-m\lambda-(m-1).
\]
Then
\[
P_m(1)=-2(m-1)<0,
\qquad
P_m(\lambda)\to+\infty\ \text{as }\lambda\to+\infty,
\]
and
\[
P_m'(\lambda)=m(\lambda^{m-1}-1)
\]
is negative on \((0,1)\) and positive on \((1,\infty)\). Therefore \(P_m\)
has a unique positive root \(\lambda_m>1\).

For the perturbed germ \(S(x)=x^m+O(x^{m+1})\), divide \(H_3(-\alpha,\lambda\alpha)\)
by \(\alpha^m\). The resulting equation is
\[
P_m(\lambda)+O(\alpha)=0.
\]
If \(m\) is even, positivity of the model factor persists for \(\alpha\) small,
so there is still no branch. If \(m\) is odd, the root \(\lambda_m\) is simple,
so the implicit function theorem yields a unique analytic branch
\[
\lambda=\lambda(\alpha)=\lambda_m+O(\alpha),
\]
equivalently
\[
u=\lambda_m(-a)+O(a^2).
\]
This proves the classification.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Nonmixed \(4\)-point zeros can carry preexisting close branches]
\label{rem:nonmixed-four-point-zeros-can-carry-preexisting-branches}
A blanket local theorem excluding preexisting close \(4\)-point branches near
nonmixed finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros is false in generic lifted geometry.
Indeed, the model
\[
Q(x)=(x^4,x,x^2)
\]
satisfies
\[
K_v\neq 0,
\qquad
T_v\sim x,
\]
yet the exact coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for
exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ 2,\ 4,
\]
hence factors as
\[
\Delta_4=\pm V_4\,e_1,
\qquad
e_1(x_1,x_2,x_3,x_4)=x_1+x_2+x_3+x_4.
\]
Thus there are exact shrinking coplanar quadruples near \(0\), for example any
distinct
\[
x_1<x_2<x_3<0<x_4,
\qquad
x_1+x_2+x_3+x_4=0.
\]
So on the lifted \(4\)-point side, the strongest generic local statements are
the shrinking-core concentration into \(\{T_v=0\}\), the parity-based
birth/crossing classification, and the mixed-locus analysis, not a blanket
no-preexisting-branch theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: stratified lifted local picture]
\label{rem:wip-stratified-lifted-local-picture}
The lifted local obstruction now splits into three regimes.

First, exact shrinking lifted \(3\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
K_v=0,
\]
and near a finite-order isolated \(K_v\)-zero the repeated-node
tangent-contact branch is completely classified: even order gives no
opposite-side branch, while odd order gives exactly one opposite-side branch.

Second, exact shrinking lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
T_v=0.
\]
On the nonmixed side \(K_v\neq 0\), finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros control local
birth/crossing by parity, but generic models show that a preexisting close
branch can still exist near certain odd-order nonmixed zeros. Thus the
nonmixed \(4\)-point side is not governed by a blanket local-exclusion
theorem.

Third, the mixed case
\[
K_v=T_v=0
\]
is genuinely different. After affine normalization with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
as local coordinate, the lifted space curve is led to a monomial model
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\]
and the leading \(4\)-point coplanarity determinant becomes the generalized
Vandermonde for exponents
\[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
\]
For some exponent patterns this model does admit opposite-side quadruples, so
the mixed locus remains the genuinely new codimension-two local obstruction.

Thus the remaining lifted local issues are:
the continuation / non-recurrence of the unique odd-order \(3\)-point branch,
the continuation / non-recurrence of nonmixed \(4\)-point branches, possible
infinite-order flatness, and the mixed codimension-two locus.
\end{remark}

strengthened invariant \(\widehat\Psi\), and on good \(M\neq 0\) patches this
forces bad two-pair cores into a defect-scale close regime. For the two-point
branch, the sharp remaining algebraic target is the source-level structural
reduction of the raw corrected interaction remainder: if the corrected
two-pair object is defined source-level and collapses on coincident atoms,

is excluded on compact good patches.

What I would not add yet

I would also not add a theorem claiming the two-point branch is already finished unconditionally. That still needs the source-level corrected quotient-germ map QQ, or an equivalent direct proof of the raw structural properties.

\begin{remark}[Mixed order bookkeeping and lack of generic parity obstruction]
\label{rem:mixed-order-bookkeeping-no-generic-parity-obstruction}
At a mixed lifted point
\[
K_v(0)=0,
\qquad
T_v(0)=0,
\]
the current affine-normalized model is
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\qquad
m\ge 3,
\qquad
n>m.
\]
If
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v,
\qquad
s:=\ord_0 T_v,
\]
then the model exponents satisfy
\[
r=m-2,
\qquad
s=m+n-5,
\]
hence
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3,
\qquad
s\ge 2r.
\]

The immediately dangerous parity sector in the mixed model is
\[
n\ \text{even}
\qquad\Longleftrightarrow\qquad
s-r\ \text{odd}.
\]

However, generic smooth lifted geometry imposes no further parity restriction.
Indeed, the smooth local model
\[
c(x)\equiv 1,
\qquad
v_5(x)=1+x,
\qquad
S(x)=x^m,
\qquad
Y(x)=x^n
\]
lies on a good \(v_5\)-patch and realizes arbitrary integers
\[
m\ge 3,
\qquad
n>m,
\]
hence arbitrary order pairs
\[
r\ge 1,
\qquad
s\ge 2r.
\]

Thus any exclusion of dangerous mixed patterns must come from RH-specific jet
identities or from additional algebraic compatibility conditions for true bad
four-point cores, not from generic lifted differential geometry alone.
\end{remark}

Edit 3: insert the “next four-point target” remark
Insert immediately after the mixed-order bookkeeping remark above

\begin{remark}[Next algebraic target on the four-point branch]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
The lifted four-point geometry shows that generic coplanarity alone is too
weak: nonmixed odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros can already support a preexisting close
branch, and the mixed model can admit dangerous generalized-Vandermonde
coplanar quadruples.

Accordingly, the next algebraic target for the bad four-point core is not
another generic local exclusion theorem, but an extra compatibility condition
coming from the source-level corrected finite-core relation itself. The right
question is therefore:

\begin{quote}
What additional algebraic condition does a true bad four-point core impose on a
local lifted coplanarity branch, beyond the vanishing of the lifted four-point
determinant?
\end{quote}

Any successful closure of the four-point branch will have to use that extra
compatibility condition, or else rule out the dangerous mixed exponent patterns
by RH-specific jet identities.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: what remains in the lifted order-$7$ geometry]
\label{rem:wip-lifted-order7-zero-capture}
The lifted \(v_5\)-patch geometry now splits more sharply than a blanket
zero-capture problem.

First, Propositions~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-three-point-circuits-force-Kv-zero}
and~\ref{prop:shrinking-exact-lifted-four-point-circuits-force-Tv-zero} show
that shrinking exact lifted three-point and four-point circuits can accumulate
only at
\[
K_v=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad

different. On the nonmixed side, generic odd-order \(T_v\)-zeros can carry a

bookkeeping is
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3,
\qquad
s\ge 2r,
\]
and there is no generic parity obstruction beyond this order inequality.

Thus the missing global ingredient is no longer a single blanket first-contact
lemma. It is a combination of:
\begin{itemize}
\item source-level control of the multi-pair interaction defects
\[
E_{\ge2}^{(3)},\qquad E_{\ge2}^{(5)},\qquad \overline E_{\ge2}^{(7)};
\]
\item extra algebraic compatibility conditions for true bad four-point cores,
beyond generic coplanarity of the lifted points;
\item and, on the mixed side, RH-specific jet restrictions excluding the
dangerous exponent patterns.
\end{itemize}
\end{remark}

K_v=0,
\]
and near a finite-order isolated \(K_v\)-zero the repeated-node tangent-contact
branch is completely classified: even order gives no opposite-side branch,
while odd order gives exactly one opposite-side branch.

Second, exact shrinking lifted \(4\)-point circuits concentrate into
\[
T_v=0.
\]
On the nonmixed side \(K_v\neq 0\), finite-order \(T_v\)-zeros control local
birth/crossing by parity, but generic models show that a preexisting close
branch can still exist near certain odd-order nonmixed zeros. Thus the
nonmixed \(4\)-point side is not governed by a blanket local-exclusion
theorem.

Third, the mixed case
\[
K_v=T_v=0
\]
is genuinely different. After affine normalization with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
as local coordinate, the lifted space curve is led to a monomial model
\[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,x,x^m),
\]
with order bookkeeping
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=s-r+3,
\qquad
s\ge 2r.
\]
No generic parity obstruction is available at this level, so the mixed locus
remains the genuinely new codimension-two local obstruction.

Thus the remaining lifted local issues are:
the continuation / non-recurrence of the unique odd-order \(3\)-point branch,
the continuation / non-recurrence of nonmixed \(4\)-point branches, possible
infinite-order flatness, and the mixed codimension-two locus together with the
extra bad-core compatibility conditions needed there.
\end{remark}

[

]

Second, **collapse on partial diagonals**: whenever two atoms coincide, the (4)-atom source reduces to a (3)-atom source, so the pure (4)-body remainder should vanish.

Third, **vanishing when any amplitude is zero**.

Those are the exact (4)-point analogues of the (2)-point structural conditions in the note. And if they hold, then the pure (4)-body remainder should inherit very strong divisibility:

* by (\prod_j a_j) from amplitude collapse,
* and by every pair difference (h_i-h_j) from partial-diagonal collapse.

Because the object is symmetric, vanishing on each partial diagonal should force divisibility by the **discriminant**
[
\prod_{i<j}(h_i-h_j)^2
]
rather than just a single linear factor. That is the (4)-point analogue of the midpoint/separation evenness argument in the (2)-point note. I would not claim this as proved yet, but structurally it is exactly the kind of theorem to attack.

And this would be a big deal, because it would give the extra algebraic condition you asked for:

> a true bad (4)-point core is not merely coplanar on (Q_v); it lies on a coplanarity branch along which a much more singular source-level (4)-body remainder vanishes.

That is exactly the kind of restriction that a generic local branch sheet like the nonmixed odd-order model
[

]
will probably **not** satisfy automatically.

I attacked that on both local model types.

---

## 1. Test on the nonmixed odd-order branch sheet

Near a nonmixed odd-order (T_v)-zero, we already reduced the local exact branch sheet to the normalized model
[

\qquad n \ \text{even},
]
with the exact opposite-side branch parameterized on the scale
[
a=-t,\qquad b=-(1-\rho)t,\qquad u=pt,\qquad v=q(t,\rho,p)t,
]
for small (t>0). The full exact lifted (4)-point coplanarity determinant scales as
[
\Delta_4 \sim t^{,n+3}.
]
This is the model order we already identified when classifying the nonmixed odd-order sheet. 

Now on that same cone, every pair difference is (O(t)), so the discriminant-squared factor in the hypothetical source-level remainder scales like
[
\prod_{i<j}(h_i-h_j)^2 \sim t^{12}.
]
Therefore the pure (4)-body correction scales like
[
\mathcal I_4 = O(t^{12})
]
up to the amplitude factor.

So the comparison is:

* geometric coplanarity branch term: (t^{,n+3}),
* source-level pure (4)-body correction: (t^{12}).

Hence:

### If (n+3<12), i.e. (n\le 8),

the pure (4)-body correction is **higher order** than the branch equation.

That means it cannot kill the local branch; it only perturbs it. Since the odd-order nonmixed branch sheet already has a nondegenerate implicit-function parameterization, the sheet persists under such a higher-order perturbation.

So the low-order dangerous nonmixed cases
[
n=4,\ 6,\ 8
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\ord T_v = 1,\ 3,\ 5
]
are **robust** against any extra (4)-body obstruction of discriminant-squared type.

Only when
[
n\ge 10
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\ord T_v\ge 7
]
could the extra (4)-body term enter at equal or lower order and potentially matter.

This is already a strong conclusion: the source-level (4)-body correction, even if it exists exactly as hoped, cannot eliminate the low-order nonmixed odd branch sheets.

---

## 2. Test on the mixed normal form

At a mixed point (K_v=T_v=0), the normalized model is
[
Q_v(x)\sim (x^n,\ x,\ x^m),
\qquad m\ge 3,\quad n>m,
]
and the leading (4)-point coplanarity determinant is the generalized Vandermonde for exponents
[
0,\ 1,\ m,\ n.
]
Its total scaling order on a shrinking opposite-side quadruple is
[
t^{,m+n+1},
]
because the Vandermonde contributes (t^6) and the Schur factor contributes degree (m+n-5). This is exactly the mixed order count already implicit in the other chat’s monomial analysis. 

Again, the source-level pure (4)-body correction contributes order
[
t^{12}.
]

So:

### If (m+n+1<12), i.e. (m+n\le 10),

the discriminant-squared (4)-body correction is again **higher order** than the mixed coplanarity equation.

Therefore it cannot remove those mixed dangerous local branches either; it only deforms them.

So all low-order mixed dangerous patterns with
[
m+n\le 10
]
are also robust against this kind of extra algebraic condition.

Only in the high-order mixed regime
[
m+n\ge 11
]
could the source-level (4)-body remainder enter at competitive order.

---

## 3. What this means

This is the real attack result:

[
\boxed{
\text{Even if a pure source-level (4)-body remainder exists with discriminant-squared factorization, it cannot kill the low-order dangerous (4)-point branches.}
}
]

So the extra algebraic condition you wanted **does exist in principle**, but after testing it on the actual local models, it turns out to be too high-order to eliminate the low-order dangerous branches.

That means:

* it is still worth formulating the pure (4)-body remainder theorem, because it is the correct source-level structure;
* but it will only matter in sufficiently high-order local regimes;
* the genuinely dangerous low-order nonmixed odd sheets and low-order mixed sheets must be ruled out, if at all, by **RH-specific jet restrictions**, not by generic discriminant-squared (4)-body algebra.

Yes. Here is a clean math formalization of the conditional pure 4-body remainder theorem and the low-order robustness corollary.

I will keep it entirely at the level of rigorous statements and proofs, with the minimum assumptions needed.
1. Source-level setup for the pure 4-body remainder

Let GG be a finite-dimensional complex vector space, and let
Q:μ⟼Q(μ)∈G
Q:μ⟼Q(μ)∈G

be an analytic map defined on small finite atomic sources
μ=∑j=1Najδhj.
μ=j=1∑N​aj​δhj​​.

For every nonempty subset I⊂{1,2,3,4}I⊂{1,2,3,4}, write
μI:=∑i∈Iaiδhi,FI:=Q(μI).
μI​:=i∈I∑​ai​δhi​​,FI​:=Q(μI​).

Define the pure 4-body remainder by Möbius inversion on the subset lattice:
I4(a1,h1;… ;a4,h4):=∑∅≠I⊂{1,2,3,4}(−1) 4−∣I∣ FI.
I4​(a1​,h1​;…;a4​,h4​):=∅=I⊂{1,2,3,4}∑​(−1)4−∣I∣FI​.​

Equivalently,
I4=F1234−∑∣I∣=3FI+∑∣I∣=2FI−∑∣I∣=1FI.
I4​=F1234​−∣I∣=3∑​FI​+∣I∣=2∑​FI​−∣I∣=1∑​FI​.
2. Conditional pure 4-body factorization theorem

The right structural theorem is this.
Theorem

Assume:

    QQ is analytic in the amplitudes and support positions.

    QQ is source-symmetric, so Q(μ)Q(μ) depends only on the atomic source and not on the ordering of the labeled atoms.

    The pure 4-body remainder vanishes on every partial diagonal:
    for every 1≤i<j≤41≤i<j≤4,
    I4(a1,h1;… ;ai,h;… ;aj,h;… ;a4,h4)=0.
    I4​(a1​,h1​;…;ai​,h;…;aj​,h;…;a4​,h4​)=0.

Then there exists an analytic GG-valued germ J4J4​ such that
I4=(∏j=14aj)(∏1≤i<j≤4(hi−hj)2) J4.
I4​=(j=1∏4​aj​)(1≤i<j≤4∏​(hi​−hj​)2)J4​.​

So the pure 4-body remainder carries both a full amplitude factor and a discriminant-squared factor.
Proof

We break it into three steps.
Step 1: divisibility by ∏jaj∏j​aj​

Fix k∈{1,2,3,4}k∈{1,2,3,4}. If ak=0ak​=0, then for every subset J⊂{1,2,3,4}∖{k}J⊂{1,2,3,4}∖{k},
FJ∪{k}=FJ,
FJ∪{k}​=FJ​,

because the kk-th atom contributes nothing to the source.

Therefore in the inclusion–exclusion sum for I4I4​, the terms indexed by JJ and J∪{k}J∪{k} cancel pairwise:
(−1)4−∣J∣FJ+(−1)4−(∣J∣+1)FJ∪{k}=0.
(−1)4−∣J∣FJ​+(−1)4−(∣J∣+1)FJ∪{k}​=0.

Hence
I4=0whenever ak=0.

I attacked it as far as the current draft and the recent notes allow, and the clean result is this:

For the **nonmixed (4)-point branch**, the local problem reduces exactly to a jet theorem for one scalar function. Near a point with
[
T_v(0)=0,\qquad K_v(0)\neq 0,
]
the lifted curve
[
Q_v=(Y,x,S),\qquad Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\quad S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5},
]
can be affinely normalized so that
[
Q_v(x)=(\widetilde Y(x),,x,,x^2),
]
because when (K_v\neq 0), the lower triple ((1,x,S)) is already disconjugate and (S) is a genuine quadratic coordinate to first order. In this normalization, the lifted (4)-point Wronskian becomes
[
T_v=W_x(1,\widetilde Y,x,x^2)=2,\widetilde Y'''.
]
So the dangerous nonmixed odd-order branch is nothing more and nothing less than an **odd-order zero of (\widetilde Y''')**.

That makes the low-order dangerous cases completely explicit:

* (n=4) means
  [
  \widetilde Y'''(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)\neq 0;
  ]
* (n=6) means
  [
  \widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(4)}(0)=\widetilde Y^{(5)}(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(6)}(0)\neq 0;
  ]
* (n=8) means
  [
  \widetilde Y^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=\widetilde Y^{(7)}(0)=0,\qquad \widetilde Y^{(8)}(0)\neq 0.
  ]

So the nonmixed (4)-pair problem has now been reduced to this very sharp statement:

[

}
]

[

Yes. Going only from what is already in the current file, the strongest exact lifted (4)-point identities you can derive are these. The file gives the lifted patch variables
[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\sigma_v=\frac{\Delta_7}{c,v_5},
]
together with
[
K_v=x'\sigma_v''-\sigma_v'x'',
\qquad
T_v=W_h(1,Y,x,S). ; ;
]

Now treat (x) as the local coordinate on a good (v_5)-patch, so (x'(h)\neq 0). Writing (S=S(x)), chain rule gives
[
\sigma_v'(h)=S_x,x',
\qquad
\sigma_v''(h)=S_{xx}(x')^2+S_x x'',
]
hence
[
K_v
===

# x'\sigma_v''-\sigma_v' x''

(x')^3 S_{xx}.
]
So the exact coordinate relation is
[
\boxed{K_v=(x')^3,S''(x).}
]
In particular, (K_v) and (S'') have the same zero set and the same vanishing order on a good patch. This is the precise version of the “(K_v) is (S'') up to a nowhere-zero factor” statement already used in the file.

For (T_v), use the reparametrization formula for Wronskians of four functions:
[
W_h(1,Y,x,S)=(x')^6,W_x(1,Y,x,S).
]
A direct determinant expansion gives
[
W_x(1,Y,x,S)
============

\det!\begin{pmatrix}
1&Y&x&S\
0&Y'&1&S'\
0&Y''&0&S''\
0&Y'''&0&S'''
\end{pmatrix}
=============

S''Y'''-S'''Y''.
]
Therefore
[
\boxed{T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr).}
]
Equivalently,
[
\boxed{T_v=(x')^6,S''^{,2},\frac{d}{dx}!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).}
]
Since (K_v=(x')^3S''), this can also be written as
[
\boxed{T_v=K_v^{,2},\frac{d}{dx}!\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right).}
]
That is the cleanest identity in the file for the lifted (4)-point branch. It is stronger than the bare statement “(T_v=W_h(1,Y,x,S)).”

This immediately gives the exact nonmixed reduction. If (K_v(0)\neq 0), then after affine normalization of the lower triple ((1,x,S)) you may take
[
S=x^2,
\qquad
S''=2,
\qquad
S'''=0,
]
so the identity becomes
[
\boxed{T_v=2(x')^6,Y'''.}
]
Thus at a nonmixed point, the dangerous low-order branch cases are exactly the odd-order zeros of (Y'''). In particular:
[
\ord_0 T_v=1 \iff Y'''(0)=0,\ Y^{(4)}(0)\neq 0,
]
[
\ord_0 T_v=3 \iff Y^{(3)}(0)=Y^{(4)}(0)=Y^{(5)}(0)=0,\ Y^{(6)}(0)\neq 0,
]
[
\ord_0 T_v=5 \iff Y^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=Y^{(7)}(0)=0,\ Y^{(8)}(0)\neq 0.
]
So the nonmixed (4)-point obstruction has been reduced to a jet theorem for one scalar germ (Y=u_5/c) after normalizing (S) to (x^2).

For the mixed case, let
[
r:=\ord_0 K_v.
]
Since (K_v=(x')^3S''), one has
[
S''(x)=\kappa x^r+O(x^{r+1}),
\qquad \kappa\neq 0.
]
After removing affine terms and integrating twice,
[
\boxed{S(x)=\frac{\kappa}{(r+1)(r+2)}x^{r+2}+O(x^{r+3}).}
]
So the mixed exponent (m) is exactly
[
\boxed{m=r+2.}
]

Now write the first term of (Y) not absorbed by (\operatorname{span}{1,x,S}) as
[
Y(x)=\alpha x^n+O(x^{n+1}),
\qquad \alpha\neq 0,\qquad n>r+2.
]
Substituting into
[
T_v=(x')^6\bigl(S''Y'''-S'''Y''\bigr)
]
gives
[
S''Y'''-S'''Y''
===============

\kappa\alpha,n(n-1)\bigl(n-r-2\bigr)x^{n+r-3}+O(x^{n+r-2}),
]
so
[
\boxed{\ord_0 T_v=n+r-3.}
]
If (s:=\ord_0 T_v), this becomes
[
\boxed{n=s-r+3,}
]
which is exactly the mixed bookkeeping relation already recorded in the recent notes. ; ;

The same identity also yields a cleaner invariant quantity:
[
\boxed{
\ord_0!\left(\frac{d}{dx}\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)\right)=s-2r.
}
]
So the low-order dangerous mixed cases are not abstract anymore. They are exactly
[
(r,s)\in{(1,2),(1,4),(2,5)},
]
equivalently
[
(m,n)\in{(3,4),(3,6),(4,6)},
]
equivalently
[
\ord_0!\left(\frac{d}{dx}\left(\frac{Y''}{S''}\right)\right)\in{0,2,1}.
]
That is the finite list of low-order mixed jet obstructions currently visible from the file. ; ;

So the exact identities you can really extract from the current draft are:

[

Partial septic oddness theorem

[Δ7][1](s) is odd in s.

Why this is true

s↦−s.

    Quintic fixed-sector: not yet fully reduced to a centered low-jet parity statement.

Yes. Here is the actual groundwork you can use.

The right move is to work in the centered symmetric-placement variable
t±=h±s2,

and treat s↦−ss↦−s as swapping the two microscopic points. Then every 2×22×2 symmetric coefficient matrix

satisfies
an(−s)=cn(s),bn(−s)=bn(s),cn(−s)=an(s).
an​(−s)=cn​(s),bn​(−s)=bn​(s),cn​(−s)=an​(s).

So define the even/odd half-sum/half-difference variables
aˉn:=an+cn2(even),δan:=cn−an2(odd),
aˉn​:=2an​+cn​​(even),δan​:=2cn​−an​​(odd),

and similarly for every diagonal pair, while the off-diagonal entry is always even.

5. Important caveat

This is in the symmetric-placement separation variable ss.

It is not yet the same thing as the local coordinate on a good v5v5​-patch used later for the lifted 44-point branch, and that mismatch is exactly why the earlier “odd Δ7Δ7​” dream package was off. What we have now is the correct raw Taylor groundwork in the natural symmetric variable.

So the next translation step, if you want to keep pushing, is:

u5​, v5​, u7,K1​​, v7,K1​​, Δ7​.

That yields concrete low-order septic coefficients
D2, D4, D6
D2​, D4​, D6​

rather than just a parity slogan. That is worth keeping.

A second useful point is the exact local factorization at the diagonal-centered odd/odd model:
Y(x)=xnB(x2),S(x)=xmA(x2),
Y(x)=xnB(x2),S(x)=xmA(x2),

with m,nm,n odd, and then
S′′(x)=xm−2Σm[A](x2),Z(x)=xn−mH(x2),R(x)=xn−m−1J(x2).
S′′(x)=xm−2Σm​[A](x2),Z(x)=xn−mH(x2),R(x)=xn−m−1J(x2).

This is better than the earlier informal discussion because it gives a real punctured-neighborhood exclusion:
for sufficiently small nonzero xx,
Kv(x)≠0,Tv(x)≠0.
Kv​(x)=0,Tv​(x)=0.

That is a solid local theorem near the centered diagonal base, and I would definitely keep it.

A third useful item is the clearer fork in the involution route. The summary isolates the dependence of the quintic commutator channel on the parity of the cubic matrix coefficient X3X3​:
if X1X1​ is odd and X3X3​ is odd, the commutator contribution to A5fA5f​ is even; if X3X3​ is even, it is odd. That is a real sharpening of where the descent problem sits. It tells you exactly what parity datum the current draft still does not resolve.

The one part I would treat cautiously is the claim that centered symmetric-placement parity, after passing to
x=v5c,
x=cv5​​,

forces
Y(x) odd,S(x) odd,Z(x) even,R(x) odd,
Y(x) odd,S(x) odd,Z(x) even,R(x) odd,

and therefore kills the whole low-order mixed list. This is promising, but it crosses from the diagonal collision-side variable ss into the good-patch xx-chart, and that bridge is exactly where parity arguments have already proved delicate. I would keep that as a strong candidate theorem, not yet as settled fact, until the coordinate transfer is checked line by line.

So my bottom line is:

The genuinely useful additions are the explicit D2,D4,D6D2​,D4​,D6​ septic coefficients, the punctured-neighborhood exclusion near the centered diagonal base, and the sharpened X3X3​-parity fork in the involution route.

The potentially very important but still provisional addition is the claim that the centered-ss parity package kills the full explicit low-order mixed 44-point list after transfer to x=v5/cx=v5​/c. That one deserves a careful re-check before it gets promoted.

Edit 1: add the below-lifted Wronskian-ratio reformulation

Insert this block immediately after the theorem/proposition where the draft first introduces the exact identities
Kv=(x′)3S′′(x),Tv=(x′)6(S′′Y′′′−S′′′Y′′),
Kv​=(x′)3S′′(x),Tv​=(x′)6(S′′Y′′′−S′′′Y′′),

and before the next discussion of nonmixed/mixed local models.

Use:

\begin{remark}[Below-lifted Wronskian-ratio reformulation]
\label{rem:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-reformulation}
Let
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\qquad
\lambda:=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
M:=cv_5'-c'v_5.
\]
For any scalar germ \(f\), define
\[
J_f(h):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
c(h)&v_5(h)&f(h)\\
c'(h)&v_5'(h)&f'(h)\\
c''(h)&v_5''(h)&f''(h)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\frac{d^2}{dx^2}\!\left(\frac{f}{c}\right)
=
\frac{c^3}{M^3}\,J_f.
\]
Applying this to \(f=u_5\) and \(f=\lambda\) gives
\[
Y''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{u_5},
\qquad
S''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{\lambda},
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z:=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_{\lambda}}.
}
\]
Differentiating in the \(x\)-coordinate yields
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal R:=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
=
\frac{c^2}{M}\frac{d}{dh}\!\left(\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_{\lambda}}\right).
}
\]
Thus the lifted \(4\)-point branch may be viewed equivalently as a
parity/divisibility problem for the Wronskian ratio \(J_{u_5}/J_{\lambda}\).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[A second below-lifted ratio does not add a new obstruction]
\label{rem:second-below-lifted-ratio-no-new-obstruction}
Let
\[
\Theta:=\frac{W_{u_5}}{W},
\]
where \(W\) denotes the corresponding projective-chart Wronskian in the
\((c,v_5,\cdot)\)-frame. In the gauge \(c\equiv 1\), \(v_5=x\), one has the
exact relation
\[
\Theta=\mathcal Z\,\frac{S''}{xS''+2S'},
\qquad
(\mathcal Z-x\Theta)S''=2\Theta S'.
\]
So \(\Theta\) does not provide an independent local obstruction beyond
\((\mathcal Z,\mathcal R)\): whenever \(2\Theta/(\mathcal Z-x\Theta)\) is
analytic, one can solve locally for \(S\) and then recover \(Y\) from
\(Y''=\mathcal Z S''\). In particular, attacks based only on a generic
differential relation between \(\mathcal Z\) and \(\Theta\) are too weak to
close the \(4\)-point branch.
\end{remark}

This captures the solid “below-lifted” identity and the no-go result about ΘΘ.
Edit 2: add the exact finite obstruction coefficients for the nonmixed and mixed 44-point branches

Use:

\begin{remark}[Exact finite obstruction coefficients for the low-order \(4\)-point branch]
\label{rem:exact-finite-obstruction-coefficients-low-order-four-point}
The explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list can be reduced to a finite
jet package.

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed side.}
Suppose \(K_v(0)\neq 0\), and write
\[
s_k:=S^{(k)}(0),
\qquad
y_k:=Y^{(k)}(0),
\qquad
s_2\neq 0.
\]
Then the Taylor expansion
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=z_0+z_1x+z_2x^2+z_3x^3+z_4x^4+z_5x^5+z_6x^6+O(x^7)
\]
has canonical even coefficients
\[
z_2,\qquad z_4,\qquad z_6,
\]
and the dangerous nonmixed low-order cases are exactly:
\[
n=4 \iff z_2\neq 0,
\qquad
n=6 \iff z_2=0,\ z_4\neq 0,
\qquad
n=8 \iff z_2=z_4=0,\ z_6\neq 0.
\]
Explicitly,
\[
z_2=
\frac{
s_2^2y_4-2s_2s_3y_3+\bigl(2s_3^2-s_2s_4\bigr)y_2
}{
2\,s_2^3
},
\]
\[
z_4=
\frac{
s_2^4y_6
-s_2^3(4s_3y_5+6s_4y_4+4s_5y_3+s_6y_2)
+2s_2^2(6s_3^2y_4+12s_3s_4y_3+4s_3s_5y_2+3s_4^2y_2)
-12s_2s_3^2(2s_3y_3+3s_4y_2)
+24s_3^4y_2
}{
24\,s_2^5
},
\]
and
\[
z_6=\frac{\mathcal P_8(s_2,\dots,s_8;y_2,\dots,y_8)}{720\,s_2^7},
\]
where \(\mathcal P_8\) is the explicit degree-\(8\) numerator polynomial obtained
by Taylor division of \(\mathcal Z=Y''/S''\).

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Mixed side.}
Suppose \(K_v(0)=T_v(0)=0\), and let
\[
r:=\ord_0 K_v.
\]
For the two low-order mixed cases \(r=1,2\), Taylor division of
\(\mathcal Z=Y''/S''\) gives the exact obstruction coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2},
\]
defined by the expansions
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{y_2}{s_3}\frac1x
+
\left(\frac{y_3}{s_3}-\frac{s_4y_2}{2s_3^2}\right)
+
\kappa_{1,1}x+\kappa_{1,2}x^2+\kappa_{1,3}x^3+O(x^4)
\qquad (r=1),
\]
and
\[
\mathcal Z(x)
=
\frac{2y_2}{s_4}\frac1{x^2}
+
\left(\frac{2y_3}{s_4}-\frac{2s_5y_2}{3s_4^2}\right)\frac1x
+
\left(
\frac{y_4}{s_4}
-\frac{2s_5y_3}{3s_4^2}
-\frac{s_6y_2}{6s_4^2}
+\frac{2s_5^2y_2}{9s_4^3}
\right)
+\kappa_{2,1}x+\kappa_{2,2}x^2+O(x^3)
\qquad (r=2).
\]
The dangerous mixed low-order list is then exactly:
\[
(m,n)=(3,4)\iff \kappa_{1,1}\neq 0,
\]
\[
(m,n)=(3,6)\iff \kappa_{1,3}\neq 0,
\]
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)\iff \kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

Thus the full currently explicit low-order \(4\)-point obstruction list is
equivalent to the finite set of coefficients
\[
\boxed{
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]
Any RH-specific local closure theorem for the \(4\)-point branch must force
these six quantities to vanish.
\end{remark}

This captures the six exact obstruction coefficients. It is one of the best “goodies” to preserve.
